Inches From Each Other: Bipartisan Group Of Senators Decry Child Migrant Facilities, Demand Press Access At Border","subhead":"","content":"\u003cp\u003eA bipartisan group of senators is calling for the Biden administration to open up press access at the United States border after viewing several child migrant detention facilities that one Senator said he would not want your child in for more than 10 minutes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe visit follows \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/NorahODonnell/status/1371953668682043404?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1371953668682043404%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_\u0026amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.dailywire.com%2Fnews%2Fbreaking-bidens-border-crisis-explodes-number-of-unaccompanied-children-in-custody-300-higher-than-previously-known\"\u003ereports that the number of child migrants\u003c/a\u003e being held at the border is more than 300 times that originally reported, and that around 13,000 unaccompanied minors are currently in United States custody, overwhelming border patrol facilities and turning the situation at the United-States-Mexico border into a humanitarian crisis.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSen. Shelley Moore Capito (R-WV), Sen. Chris Murphy (D-CT), and two others accompanied Department of Homeland Security Secretary Alejandro Mayorkas to tour an at-capacity facility housing child migrants over the weekend and found children cramped shoulder to shoulder in large rooms for far longer than the law allows.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCapito, \u0026#8220;one of four senators who accompanied Homeland Security Secretary Alejandro Mayorkas to the border, said in an interview with The Washington Post Saturday that as many as 100 migrant children were being held in a large room at one Customs and Border Protection processing center in El Paso amid the coronavirus pandemic,\u0026#8221; \u003ca href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/senators-border-minors-press-access/2021/03/20/c4ce50ce-89c2-11eb-8a67-f314e5fcf88d_story.html\"\u003ethe outlet noted\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026#8220;More than 200 border agents have been diverted to this CBP facility to care for the children, Capito said. The children, who arrived at the southern border without a parent, are legally allowed to be held for only 72 hours in CBP custody before being transferred elsewhere. But many are there for days longer than that,\u0026#8221; Capito told the Washington Post.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMurphy, a Democrat, was also stunned at the conditions he found at the border but was careful to continue to differentiate the situation under President Joe Biden from that under President Donald Trump, telling the Washington Post that these are not kids in so-called cages.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHe said, however, that the conditions on the border are conditions you would not want your child in for more than 10 minutes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYoure sleeping on thin mattresses on the floor. They are sort of bunched, you know, about six inches to a foot from each other, Murphy told media. Weve got to ultimately do better.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBoth Capito and Murphy encouraged the Biden administration to allow press access to border detention facilities and to lift unofficial \u0026#8220;gag orders\u0026#8221; Wire"},{"property":"article:published_time","content":"2021-03-20T17:01:31+00:00"},{"property":"article:modified_time","content":"2021-03-21T17:34:37+00:00"},{"name":"twitter:card","content":"summary_large_image"},{"name":"twitter:image","content":"https://dw-wp-production.imgix.net/2021/03/Biden-Migrants.jpg"}]},{"id":202150,"date":"2021-03-20T17:00:14","modified":"2021-03-21T17:23:23","slug":"prager-the-human-need-to-feel-important-and-how-government-squelches-it","title":"PRAGER: The Human Need To Feel Important  And How Government Squelches It","subhead":"","content":"\u003cp\u003eIf one were to draw up a list of human needs, food and shelter would be at the top.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWith great respect to Freudians, sex would not be No. 2.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe need for meaning would be second only to the need for food.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThat meaning is more important to happiness than sex is easily shown. A great many people go long periods without sex, and while many of them miss it, if they have meaning in their lives, they can lead quite happy and fulfilling lives. On the other hand, few people who have regular sex but lack meaning are happy or fulfilled.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThird on the list of human needs is the need to feel important. This need is much less often cited than the need for food, sex and meaning. But it is so important that a case could be made that it is tied for No. 2 with the need for meaning.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe infamous \u0026#8220;midlife crisis\u0026#8221; is a crisis of importance: \u0026#8220;I thought I would be much more important at this stage in life than I am.\u0026#8221; That mostly afflicts men  just as feeling less important after one\u0026#8217;s children have left home afflicts mothers more than fathers.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAmong the many psycho-social crises afflicting Americans is a crisis of importance. Fewer Americans feel important than did Americans in the past.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhy? What has happened?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhat has happened is a steep decline in the number of institutions that gave people a feeling of importance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGiven that work is generally regarded as one of the most ubiquitous providers of purpose, and that, prior to the COVID-19 lockdown, more Americans were working than ever before, one would think that more Americans than ever before felt important.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt has not turned out that way. For many, work has not provided the sense of importance people expected it to, let alone fulfilled the other great need: for meaning. This is especially true for women, but first, we will address men.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWork used to provide many men with a sense of importance. It is simply a fact that being the breadwinner for a family means one is important. However, since the 1970s and the rise of feminism, women have not only become breadwinners, but they have increasingly become the primary breadwinner within a marriage and for a family. That has helped couples financially, but it has also deprived a great many men of their sense of importance. When regarded by a wife and children as important, husbands/fathers felt important. Progressive America mocks the 1950s TV series \u0026#8220;Father Knows Best.\u0026#8221; But when wives and children believed that, men felt important because they were. The price for this, according to feminism, was paid by women, who didn\u0026#8217;t receive the accolades of breadwinning. And they set about changing it.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, contrary to the expectations of the well-educated, women becoming breadwinners has not provided most women with a sense of importance, and certainly not meaning in life. Contrary to what feminism, colleges, high schools, progressive parents and the mass media have claimed for decades, men and women do not have the same natures. Just as sex with many partners does not provide most women with the same satisfaction it provides men, most work does not provide women with the same sense of importance or meaning it provides men. For many women, being the breadwinner is financially beneficial but not especially satisfying. Most women would still like their man to be the primary breadwinner. That\u0026#8217;s why very wealthy women so often marry even wealthier men. It is built into female nature.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMoreover, throughout history, work was rarely seen as a primary provider of importance or meaning  for either sex. Work was little more than a necessity, and the vast majority of people would have happily abandoned their often back-breaking, drudgery-inducing work if they could afford to.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor the most part, people sought  and found  importance and meaning outside of work. This was especially true in America, where \u0026#8220;associations\u0026#8221; provided both importance and meaning.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNongovernmental associations, as Alexis de Tocqueville noted in his brilliant analysis of American life in the early 19th century, was the key to Americans\u0026#8217; success and happiness. These included, first and foremost, religious associations and religion in general. Most religious people feel important  to God, to their community, to their family. My father was the president of our synagogue, and my mother was active in the synagogue\u0026#8217;s \u0026#8220;sisterhood.\u0026#8221; Though both worked full time, those roles provided them with immense meaning and sense of importance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAdd to that: Rotary, Kiwanis and Lions clubs; book clubs; the Masons; bowling leagues; coaching Little League; volunteer charitable work; teaching Bible in Sunday school. These provided people with a sense of importance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe key to all these associations was their being independent of government. As government has grown, nearly all these associations have shrunk. Therefore, we have a rule: The more government intrudes in people\u0026#8217;s lives, the less important most people feel  unless they work for the government.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYet, to progressives, government is, or should be, almost everything in people\u0026#8217;s lives. It should take care of as many people as possible. However, at a massive price: The more one relies on the government, the more one will inevitably lack a sense of importance.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis ideal was announced at the 2012 Democratic Party Convention, when the narrator of a specially-created Barack Obama campaign-theme video asserted, \u0026#8220;Government is the only thing that we all belong to.\u0026#8221; The DNC also showed a fictional storybook ad titled \u0026#8220;The Life of Julia.\u0026#8221; It portrayed a woman from childhood to old age, wholly dependent on the government. Despite her having a child, there was not a man anywhere in the story, nor, apparently, was there a man in her life. The result? More and more American women have come to rely on the government, not on a husband. The results have been calamitous.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePresident Joe Biden repeated this theme last week: \u0026#8220;Put trust and faith in our government,\u0026#8221; he pleaded with Americans. One could accurately say that we are replacing America\u0026#8217;s motto, \u0026#8220;In God We Trust,\u0026#8221; with, \u0026#8220;In Government We Trust.\u0026#8221;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe bigger the government, the fewer the institutions in which people can feel important. Therefore, given the deep human need to feel important, people will look elsewhere for their importance  like fighting systemic racism, heteronormativity, capitalism, patriarchy and transphobia. And, most of all, global warming  because you cannot feel more important than when you believe you are saving the world.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ci\u003eThe views expressed in this opinion piece are the authors own and do not necessarily represent those of The Daily Wire.\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ci\u003eDennis Prager is a nationally syndicated radio talk-show host and columnist. His latest book, published by Regnery in May 2019, is \u0026#8220;The Rational Bible,\u0026#8221; a commentary on the book of Genesis. His film, \u0026#8220;No Safe Spaces,\u0026#8221; was released to home entertainment nationwide on September 15, 2020. He became a contributing opinion writer for The New York Times.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe paranoia overflowed from this self-described \u0026#8220;professional Black person\u0026#8221; on St. Patrick\u0026#8217;s Day. Young posted a piece titled \u0026#8220;Whiteness Is a Pandemic.\u0026#8221; This was not a joke. It began: \u0026#8220;Whiteness is a public health crisis. It shortens life expectancies, it pollutes air, it constricts equilibrium, it devastates forests, it melts ice caps, it sparks (and funds) wars, it flattens dialects, it infests consciousnesses, and it kills people  white people and people who are not white, my mom included. There will be people who die, in 2050, because of white supremacy-induced decisions from 1850.\u0026#8221;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe can all imagine what might happen professionally to a writer if he were to pen this kind of foam-flecked copy but instead talk about \u0026#8220;Blackness.\u0026#8221; It\u0026#8217;d be denounced as virulently racist. But to hate everything about the infestation of Caucasians is not defined as \u0026#8220;hate speech.\u0026#8221; It\u0026#8217;s somehow \u0026#8220;anti-racist.\u0026#8221;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis article ended the same way: \u0026#8220;White supremacy is a virus that, like other viruses, will not die until there are no bodies left for it to infect. ","content":"\u003cp\u003eLos Angeles County District Attorney George Gascn reached his 100\u003csup\u003eth\u003c/sup\u003e day in office on Wednesday and held a virtual press conference touting his policy changes that shook up the nations largest criminal justice jurisdiction.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSince I took office, Ive instituted a series of reforms based on data and science that will enhance the safety of our community while reducing racial disparities and the misuse of incarceration, Gascn said. Our efforts to transform a dated approach that creates more crime, more victims, and inequities are just beginning.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAfter Gascn took the oath on December 7, he announced a set of special directives that sparked an immediate revolt from deputy DAs in his own office, as well as families impacted by violent crime, and motivated a recall effort.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOne of his most controversial moves was ending all sentencing enhancements, which act as extra punishments added on to an underlying charge. The order, which was not part of his campaign platform, banned prosecutors from filing enhancements and required they be withdrawn from pending matters. A public outcry helped persuade Gascn to re-evaluate that directive and swiftly reinstated the use of some enhancements for cases involving the most vulnerable victims. Still, there are more than 100 enhancements in Californias penal code.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEnhancements are no longer sought in most cases as research suggests that excessive sentences dont enhance safety but do exacerbate recidivism, leading to more victims of crime, Gascn said during the news conference.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGascn cited statistics that compared his first three months in office to the same period last year, which he said showed a 71% reduction in enhancements filed. He said the drop eliminated over 8,000 years of unnecessary prison exposure time.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"500\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eEliminated 8,127 years of unnecessary, excessive and expensive exposure to prison time. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eStopped seeking the death penalty in 17 cases.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWithdrew 77 pending motions to transfer kids to adult court.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSaved taxpayers hundreds of millions of dollars.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll during my first 100 days. \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/I5XaIZveb7\"\u003epic.twitter.com/I5XaIZveb7\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; George Gascn (@GeorgeGascon) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/GeorgeGascon/status/1372990725994938369?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\"\u003eMarch 19, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTaking a new approach to promote ending enhancements, Gascn claimed the strategy eased the burden on taxpayers, saying cost savings are projected to be in the hundreds of millions of dollars.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eLAist \u003ca href=\"https://laist.com/latest/post/20210317/los-angeles-da-george-gascon-in-3-months-cut-prison-sentences-8,000-years\"\u003ereported\u003c/a\u003e, If those defendants are convicted, their shorter sentences will save the state prisons $664 million, according to Gascn.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEric Siddall, vice president of the Association of Deputy District Attorneys (ADDA), told The Daily Wire, (Gascns) math is pure fiction.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEnhancements, for the most part, are only applicable to violent criminals, Siddall continued. What he is really saying is that he is no longer prosecuting violent criminals to the fullest extent of the law.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eADDA filed a lawsuit against Gascn, alleging he had ignored laws and placed prosecutors in an ethical dilemma. Last month, a judge issued a \u003ca href=\"https://www.dailywire.com/news/judge-issues-injunction-blocking-several-directives-from-l-a-countys-new-controversial-d-a\"\u003epreliminary injunction\u003c/a\u003e ruling Gascns sentence enhancement policy violated Californias Three Strikes law, which Gascn had promised not to enforce if elected.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOn Wednesday, Gascn spotlighted his record of withdrawing 77 pending motions to transfer juveniles to adult court and establishing a Crime Victims Advisory Board to provide support during parole hearings instead of prosecutors. He said the death penalty had been taken off the table because it costs taxpayers tremendously, predicting, and soon enough, the rest of the country will follow suit.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"500\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eThe first 100 days \u0026#8211; a failure of justice: complete abandonment of the law, victims rights, public safety, personal accountability, punishment, facts and truth, human decency, and caring and empathy for all.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; jonathanhatami (@jonathanhatami) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/jonathanhatami/status/1372270155783282688?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\"\u003eMarch 17, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe first 100 days  a failure of justice: complete abandonment of the law, victims rights, public safety, personal accountability, punishment, facts and truth, human decency, and caring and empathy for all, tweeted Jon Hatami, a deputy district attorney in Gascns office who has been critical of the new direction.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHatami recently \u003ca href=\"https://www.foxla.com/news/deputy-da-files-lawsuit-against-la-da-george-gascon\"\u003efiled a lawsuit\u003c/a\u003e against Gascn alleging defamation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTania Owen, a retired detective for with L.A. County Sheriffs Department, is an honorary co-chair of the recall group. She is also the widow of slain LASD Sgt. Steve Owen, who was murdered in the line of duty in 2016.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGascn has transformed Los Angeles Countys top prosecutorial office into a public defenders office that prioritizes protecting criminals over victims, Owen \u003ca href=\"https://www.presstelegram.com/2021/03/17/la-county-district-attorney-george-gascon-marks-100-days-in-office\"\u003esaid\u003c/a\u003e in a statement. Gascn has made our most vulnerable communities less safe by eliminating sentencing enhancements for violent criminals, ending cash bail, and offering parole opportunities to cold-blooded murderers.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eD.A. Gascn insists, we are doing all of this because the science and data tells us to do so, adding, and together we can truly enhance public safety, increase equity, expand victims services, and strengthen police accountability.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, several Gascn critics have questioned the validity of the research he often \u003ca href=\"http://da.lacounty.gov/media/news/district-attorney-george-gascon-outlines-reforms-made-during-first-100-days-office-promises-more\"\u003ereferences\u003c/a\u003e, alleging the findings tend to be more anecdotal than scientific and come from like-minded progressive organizations advocating for drastic systemic reforms. On Friday, Gascn posted a string of \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/GeorgeGascon/status/1372990743594164224\"\u003etweets\u003c/a\u003e repeating the claims he made earlier this week, with citations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRelated: \u003ca href=\"https://www.dailywire.com/news/l-a-county-d-a-gascon-calls-out-conservative-media-and-tough-on-crime-types-amid-recall-threat\"\u003eL.A. The study found, \u0026#8220;Student case rates were similar in the 242 districts with 3 feet versus 6 feet of physical distancing between students \u0026#8230; Cases among school staff in districts with 3 feet versus 6 feet of physical distancing were also similar\u0026#8230;\u0026#8221;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe new updates to the \u003ca href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/community/schools-childcare/operation-strategy.html\"\u003eCDC guidelines\u003c/a\u003e include:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eRevised physical distancing recommendations to reflect at least 3 feet between students in classrooms and provide clearer guidance when a greater distance (such as 6 feet) is recommended.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eClarified that ventilation is a component of strategies to clean and maintain healthy facilities.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eRemoved recommendation for physical barriers.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eClarified the role of community transmission levels in decision-making.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cem\u003eAdded guidance on interventions when clusters occur.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe key points of the new rules dictate that there is proof that many K-12 schools that have adhered to and carried out \u0026#8220;prevention strategies\u0026#8221; have been able to welcome students back in the classroom and stay open instead of shutting down again due to outbreaks or widespread transmission of COVID-19. It added that schools should also carry out \u0026#8220;layer prevention strategies and should prioritize universal and correct use of masks and physical distancing.\u0026#8221; It also stated that testing and providing vaccinations to workers and teachers can aid in additional protection.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome states have been continuing to teach students in the classroom for many months. \u003ca href=\"https://www.dailywire.com/news/florida-reopened-their-schools-and-no-superspreaders-were-triggered-report-says\"\u003eThe Daily Wire reports\u003c/a\u003e that Florida was able to reopen its schools last August with no super-spreading outbreaks:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eRobert Runcie, the superintendent of Broward County Public Schools, the nations sixth-largest school district, echoed, If weve been able to successfully open without any major outbreaks in our schools, in a county with high infection rates, I believe that it can be done nationwide.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eLast week, Runcie stated of the fact that health and safety protocols reputedly worked to stop schools from becoming COVID-spreader environments, Given that reality, I wouldve opened schools earlier for face-to-face instruction but thats Monday morning quarterbacking in hindsight. Because we know how important face-to-face instruction is for so many of our students, we know many students are not making adequate academic progress, as NBC Miami reported.\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eDuring a White House briefing on Friday, Dr. Rochelle Walensky, director of the CDC, said that schools still need to implement other protective measures.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026#8220;These include universal and correct use of masks, physical distancing, hand washing and respiratory etiquette, cleaning to maintain healthy facilities and diagnostic testing with rapid and efficient contact tracing in combination with isolation in quarantine and in collaboration with local health departments,\u0026#8221;
